RYBAT/REDTOP/BIOGENESIS/AFEROOR - Surveillance Reports
ATTORI SUPORE
Reference: HABA-20512, dated 25 April 1969
1. Reference dispatch described our efforts against AEBOR
and stated that the next phase would consist of a 34 hour a day
surveillance of Subject for a period of about two weeks. The
coverage was initiated at 0800 hours on 19 May, and terminated
at 1515 hours on 26 May, the day of AEBOR'S departure for home
leave.
2. The overall results of the surveillance effort were
interesting, and provided us wish in a great deal of basic data which
should prove valuable in future AEBOR operational planning.
Although the period covered must be viewed as a potential local
since it covered a time of preparation for homo leave, the basic
pattern could not have varied cracly from the norm. Thore was
definite evasive action designed to shake surveillance taken by
AEBOR on several occasions; there were repeat visits to several
cases. The second could easily serve as tortor drops or con-
tact points; and there was an interesting contact on 21 May
(croported in BUENOS AIRES 3000) with an individual we failed to
identify positively.
3. Although the above makes it appear that we are approaching
the AEBOR operation -trictly from the CI/CE annule, this is not
the case. We are attempting to gather adequate information to
give us a clear insight into AEBOR'S activities in order to help
us attempt to introduce an access agent into this operation, or
to bepand direct developaent of Subject by Station officers.
4. Forwarded under separate cover for Heaquarters study
are copies of the surveillance reports along with a copy of the
ARLANTYARD transcript for 21 May,
Attachment:

REDTOF/AMEXICK/ABMOOR
Operational
References: IICSW 7566, 11 February 1969
1. With the departure of ABBOOR and his wife on home lenvo,
wo would like to offer a fow comments about him for possible future
action by the Station when he returns. The impetus for these
thoughts was a recent examination of the files of all those Boviers
and the American Society. The American Society was
offers more of a potential for intensive development than another.
The purpose of this review was not to discard the agreed-upon target
list, since this list is the rationale behind the entire concept
of selective targetting; but rather, to attempt a narrowing of the
case of the American Society. The American Society is the
best selection for operational development among the priority group.
We have looked at such factors as susceptibilities (known or
potential), contacts, accessibility, etc. and, for reasons discussed
of the American Society's "society" and the selection for a determined
Station effort inaoid at his eventual and the American's
focus on the other priority Soviets would continue at its present
level but at the sano timo. ABBOUR would be placed "under the
microscope" as the object of a more intensive Station effort aimed
at gaining multiple access to him.
2. With the incinnent departure of BIBANBET/13 from Buenos
Aéreo and tho resulting elimination of our one god contact wich
ABVULTUH, the choice of ABIOOR become easier to make. liss selection,
however, was based on several considerations which, from our
vantage point, seem to offer the base potential for Station action
when he yearned.
A. Accessibility: ABIOOR is one of the very few boxes
with whom direct Suffer contact has been made. The social
ovening sport with him and his wife in January showed excellent
promise because it appeared that foundations for rapport and
Further contact had been laid. We note, however, that there
has been no mention further meetings since the initial one,
gave the idea that the American Society was to be a
good end of Subject and his wife are not planning to reciprocate
the invitation; on the other hand, enough time will have passed
since the initial contact for the Station to take the initiative

the entire country and got to know it better than his own. He also
had various close friends in the Journalistic field including several
Americana (uic). In Mexico he was a PRAVDA correspondent.

they had a quinta to which they retired on weekends but that the
guinta was noisy and full of mosquitos. (MARGANDE and Subject's

4. Given below are MARGANDE's and LEVERONF: impressions of Subject
and wife:
Subject: Although Subject at times gives the impression of being
a rather simple fellow, this effect is created more by his apparent non-
aggressive attitude than by actual evaluation of his intelligence. He
appears to be au courant of the general situation in Argentina andhis
assessment of world situations and incidents seems to be quite logical
and unbiased. It might even be suggested that Subject is not overly influenced
by Soviet official stands concerning certain specific topics. Unlike
201-183943, he does not go about spouting a very obvious party line, Subject
presents a pleasant appearance, drowses well (he had on a clean shirt),
and is generally

individual with a fairly good sone of humor. lie apoars to understand a
fair amount of English but it is hard to judge his speaking ability since
he seems to be reluctant to talk at length in the language. He also appears

rather well but gives the impression that he has never traveled in the eastern
part of the country. From his comments and from observation it can be
assumed that he enjoys Mexican and modern American records and perhaps
even prefers time to the new, socially conscious Soviet. music. His
one detracting mannerism is a heavy and constant blink.
Subject's wife: Subject's wife is also attractive and has a warm
personality. She dresses well and is interested in theater, music and
ballot. She enjoys going to the Colon but thinks the ballet at the Dolshey
is much better. She claims to enjoy dancing and apparently does not drink
very much. Her Spanish is halting but adequate to make herself understood.
Their Relationship: Subject and nie wite appear to be a couple with,
if not in love, have grown used to each other and each other's ways.
Despite reports and direct evidence of their squabbling, it would be
dangerous to assume that this constitutes a weakness or domestic problems
They appear to rely upon each other and complement each other in social
situations to the point,there a deeper understanding between them can be
assumed. (An interest/occurence was the wife's flat declaration that
the Soviet Union was rapidly becoming a matriarchal society. Subject agreed
with a smile.) Although Subject does not take open issue with his wife
on topics where he may not be in complete accord, he manages to get his
point across with a joke and a smile. All ir all, Subject and his wife
appear to be two that could take part successfully in any social gathering.
MARGANDE thinks they are a "fun couple."

SUBJECT REDTO?/Transmittal of Soviet Personality Report, Supplement and
Characterization on Ivan Gavrilovich ALPLRYLV (201-250701)
ACTION GROUPD
REF: BUSINESS AIRLS 9897, 30 January 68
1. Forwarded herewith is a draft Soviet Personality Report,
Supplement, and Characterization on Ivan Gavrilovich ALPLRYLV
(201-236701), known AGB officer of the Fifth Department (Latin America),
First Chief Directorate (Foreign Intelligence), who served as Pravda
correspondent in Mexico City from September 1960 to October 1864.
though the draft is not in polished forms of the "SPECIAL" and "SPECIAL-1-
that it represents an accurate summaee of Subject's 201 file. lead-
quarters traces were made on Subsequent's contacts and included in the
stated Supplement. The Characterization, prepared in 1964 by Douglas
2187.10 CLASS, provides an excellent responsibility sketch of Subject and
family.
2. Throughout his tour in Mexico Subject and family remained apart
from the Soviet colony, associating chiefly with the SHUINAS (201-206547).
and the SILENGALLYS (201-328284). Subsequently, 211 temper, coarse language,
and the American American Society's design among his colleagues. (See
and characterization) Neither did ne have many known contacts among the
foreign correspondents' community. Those with whom ne did frequently
associate were representatives of Prusa Latina (PL) and Siempre. The
majority of his time was spent in CR and the American Association and
Cuba, the American Association with various leaders of the
concentrate Liberation Nacional (RLN) and central Campesina Independiente
(CCI),particularly in the rural areas of inensada, Itjamae, and
Mexicali. lie took these occasions to contact local Russian emigres and,
in one instance, to develop a rural recruiter to assess Mexican youths
desiring to study in the USSK.
Harriet J. GUILLERMINA
